    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }

      AppleID.auth.init({

  <span id="freeText3920369891355506846" style="display:none">Private investigators Liz Talbot and Nate Andrews thought they’d put Darius Baker’s troubles to rest—then his recently discovered son ropes him into a hemp farm investment with his college buddies. When a beloved Charleston professor—and potential investor—is murdered, Liz and Nate discover Darius keeps the PIs on speed dial. <br /><br />A shocking number of people had reasons to want the genteel, bowtie wearing, tea-drinking professor dead. Was it one of his many girlfriends or a disgruntled student? Or perhaps Murray was killed because his failure to invest meant the hemp farm trio’s dreams were going up in smoke?<br /><br />Though Liz’s long-dead best friend, Colleen, warns her the stakes are far higher than Liz imagines, she is hellbent on finding the no-good killer among the bevy of suspects. But will the price of justice be more than Liz can bear?</span>

<a class="leftAlignedImage userPhoto" href="/user/show/317759-kathy-wheeler"><img alt="" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/users/1343079907i/317759._UY100_CR16,0,100,100_.jpg" /></a>

<span class='communityAnswererName'>

<span class='communityAnswerText'>
My ebook copy says, “This was the most recent book in the series.” It says nothing about final. I certainly hope it’s not the final one!
</span>

<div id="review_3424256481" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3424256481" />
    <a title="Judy Lesley" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4814399-judy-lesley"><img alt="Judy Lesley" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3424256481?book_show_action=true">Jul 03, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Judy Lesley" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Judy Lesley" href="/user/show/4814399-judy-lesley">Judy Lesley</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/53451215-lowcountry-boondoggle">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4814399-judy-lesley?shelf=series">series</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4814399-judy-lesley?shelf=american">american</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4814399-judy-lesley?shelf=private-investigator">private-investigator</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3424256481" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2608765593275541298">When I open to the first page in a Liz Talbot series book I know author Susan M. Boyer will have given me that comfortable feeling for the location (Stella Maris and Charleston, South Carolina) and the family dynamics that surround Liz and her husband Nate as they tackle another case as private investigators. This one concerns the death of a local college professor who has been killed and later his home was destroyed. Liz and Nate need to find evidence of what happened and who was involved.<br/><br/>This </span>
  <span id="freeText2608765593275541298" style="display:none">When I open to the first page in a Liz Talbot series book I know author Susan M. Boyer will have given me that comfortable feeling for the location (Stella Maris and Charleston, South Carolina) and the family dynamics that surround Liz and her husband Nate as they tackle another case as private investigators. This one concerns the death of a local college professor who has been killed and later his home was destroyed. Liz and Nate need to find evidence of what happened and who was involved.<br /><br />This one has just as many descriptions as always of the classic Southern food Mrs. Talbot cooks and puts on the table when her family comes for Wednesday night dinner. Liz can't help but sense lots of undercurrents within the family members and she is determined to find out what is going on. Her father is up to something and her mother wants Liz to find out what it is. As usual, these portions of the Boyer novels make me look over my shoulder to see if she's been following me around and taking notes!<br /><br />Another solid story filled with Southern charm and atmosphere as well as good investigative practices that eventually lead to the resolution of the murder. There is a big change that happens in this book so it will be quite interesting to see how the story continues in book ten. Only a year to go until we find out.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2608765593275541298" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Lisa Hudson" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/49105261-lisa-hudson"><img alt="Lisa Hudson" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1519949806p2/49105261.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3350708620?book_show_action=true">May 30, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lisa Hudson" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lisa Hudson" href="/user/show/49105261-lisa-hudson">Lisa Hudson</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/49105261-lisa-hudson?shelf=to-be-read">to-be-read</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3350708620" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer78337651455736242">ADRENALINE OVERLOAD!<br/><br/>LOWCOUNTRY BOONDOGGLE (A Liz Talbot Mystery # 9) is finally here and it is quite the Adrenaline Overload! Author Susan M. Boyer has provided readers with her best action packed adventure to date! Be ready to find a cozy spot to relax in because once you start reading you’re not going to want to stop until you finish.<br/><br/>Everyone’s favorite married team of PIs, Liz Talbot & Nate Andrews, have been asked to work on a case that possibly involves Darius Baker’s love child. Their miss</span>
  <span id="freeText78337651455736242" style="display:none">ADRENALINE OVERLOAD!<br /><br />LOWCOUNTRY BOONDOGGLE (A Liz Talbot Mystery # 9) is finally here and it is quite the Adrenaline Overload! Author Susan M. Boyer has provided readers with her best action packed adventure to date! Be ready to find a cozy spot to relax in because once you start reading you’re not going to want to stop until you finish.<br /><br />Everyone’s favorite married team of PIs, Liz Talbot &amp; Nate Andrews, have been asked to work on a case that possibly involves Darius Baker’s love child. Their mission is to determine if he is in involved in any wrongdoing. Simple enough, right? Except the case grows much larger after they begin to investigate Brantley’s involvement in a hemp farm and the mysterious death of of one his business partner’s uncle. One thing for sure, never has one simple case ever been so full of danger! <br /><br />Boyer provides readers with all the elements she is famous for - Boyer’s eclectic cast of characters that will make you want to get out your own Murder Board; Liz’s love of family and while her own big family might drive her crazy, she will always fiercely defend them; the relationship between Liz and Nate - their mutual respect for each other’s skill set &amp; for growing together as a couple; Boyer’s plot that is always full of twists, turns, and takes you on so many goose chases you better pay attention or you’ll miss a detail; and her exquisite, detailed guide to Charleston (including the Restaurants &amp; what to order at each one). You definitely will be glad you took time to read this one! Now I will just have to rest in the knowledge that there will be more stories of Liz &amp; Nate to come!<br /><br />I was provided a complimentary copy of this book by Edelweiss &amp; Henery Press. The opinions expressed here are completely my own and without influence.</span>
  <a data-text-id="78337651455736242" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3382506490" />
    <a title="Daniele" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5869536-daniele"><img alt="Daniele" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1404873007p2/5869536.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3382506490?book_show_action=true">Jun 29, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Daniele" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Daniele" href="/user/show/5869536-daniele">Daniele</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5869536-daniele?shelf=read-2020">read-2020</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3382506490" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7630223230648383717">LOWCOUNTRY BOONDOGGLE, the ninth book in the Liz Talbot Mystery series, is as fresh and exciting as the other installments. I think it is the best book yet and is sure to please both new reader and longtime fans. This time around married couple and PI partners Liz and Nate find themselves involved with the murder of a well liked college professor. Despite his beloved status, there are plenty of secrets and suspects, including students, love interests, and family, to sift through…and, of course, </span>
  <span id="freeText7630223230648383717" style="display:none">LOWCOUNTRY BOONDOGGLE, the ninth book in the Liz Talbot Mystery series, is as fresh and exciting as the other installments. I think it is the best book yet and is sure to please both new reader and longtime fans. This time around married couple and PI partners Liz and Nate find themselves involved with the murder of a well liked college professor. Despite his beloved status, there are plenty of secrets and suspects, including students, love interests, and family, to sift through…and, of course, lots of suspense and danger.<br /><br />I tremendously enjoy Liz and Nate’s adventures. At this point in the series, each book feels like I am visiting old friends. Author Boyer does a great job balancing the wonderfully quirky characters, personal lives, and the murder mystery. I felt invested in the characters and story from the first page and did not figure out whodunit and why until very near the end.<br /><br />LOWCOUNTRY BOONDOGGLE is great fun. I look forward to many more mysteries featuring Liz Talbot. Highly recommended.<br /><br />I received an advance copy of this book from the publisher Henery Press and voluntarily shared my thoughts and opinions here. <br /></span>

          </span>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Robin Leslie Coxon" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Robin Leslie Coxon" href="/user/show/14587565-robin-leslie-coxon">Robin Leslie Coxon</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3393910747" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2776354450796414071">LowCountry Boondoggle is the ninth book in the Liz Talbot Mystery series. Talbot & Andrews Investigation returns once again with Colleen, their spirit sidekick. The law firm of Rutledge and Radcliffe have called Liz and Nate to help investigate and clear celebrity Darious Baker's son, Brantley Miller of any involvement in the recent questionable death of Dr. Murray Hamilton who was a well known and liked college professor an also the uncle to Tyler Duval. Brantley Miller, Tyler Duval and Will Ca</span>
  <span id="freeText2776354450796414071" style="display:none">LowCountry Boondoggle is the ninth book in the Liz Talbot Mystery series. Talbot &amp; Andrews Investigation returns once again with Colleen, their spirit sidekick. The law firm of Rutledge and Radcliffe have called Liz and Nate to help investigate and clear celebrity Darious Baker's son, Brantley Miller of any involvement in the recent questionable death of Dr. Murray Hamilton who was a well known and liked college professor an also the uncle to Tyler Duval. Brantley Miller, Tyler Duval and Will Capers are agriculture majors at Clemson University and are pursuing establishing a hemp farming business. The setting involves Charleston, South Carolina and surround areas. You will enjoy not just the investigation but also the feel for family involvement. Liz and Nate are very creative and yet you will get the feel of their concern for each other's safety. You will enjoy Susan Boyer's writing and her development of the characters. The characters will keep you wanting to read more and more.</span>

<div id="review_3410423785" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3410423785" />
    <a title="JoAnne McMaster (Any Good Book)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4078451-joanne-mcmaster-any-good-book"><img alt="JoAnne McMaster (Any Good Book)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1466448196p2/4078451.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3410423785?book_show_action=true">Jun 25, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="JoAnne McMaster (Any Good Book)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="JoAnne McMaster (Any Good Book)" href="/user/show/4078451-joanne-mcmaster-any-good-book">JoAnne McMaster (Any Good Book)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/53451215-lowcountry-boondoggle">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4078451-joanne-mcmaster-any-good-book?shelf=mysteries">mysteries</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4078451-joanne-mcmaster-any-good-book?shelf=supense">supense</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3410423785" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8327470433650269956">Liz Talbot and Nate Andrews are married private investigators. They've recently helped Darius Baker out of a tough spot, and now he wants them to help his son Brantley who is mixed up in a murder investigation. When his attorneys retain them to find evidence to prove Brantley innocent, they go to work.<br/><br/>Liz, however, isn't so sure that Brantley's innocent. Darius only recently discovered that he had a son, and it's because Brantley's adoptive parents were killed -- along with every other member of</span>
  <span id="freeText8327470433650269956" style="display:none">Liz Talbot and Nate Andrews are married private investigators. They've recently helped Darius Baker out of a tough spot, and now he wants them to help his son Brantley who is mixed up in a murder investigation. When his attorneys retain them to find evidence to prove Brantley innocent, they go to work.<br /><br />Liz, however, isn't so sure that Brantley's innocent. Darius only recently discovered that he had a son, and it's because Brantley's adoptive parents were killed -- along with every other member of his family -- in a suspicious fire, when none of their smoke alarms signaled anything. Even though he was never charged, she still wonders if he had anything to do with it. But being the professional she is, she's going to help him.<br /><br />It seems that Brantley, along with two buddies, have invested in a hemp farm and one of them had a college professor uncle that raised him. Tyler, from all appearances, loved his uncle and would never hurt him. But Murray was definitely poisoned, and before anyone could find evidence on his security cameras, his house was demolished in an explosion. Now Tyler is the main suspect, and Liz and Nate are on the trail of a killer -- someone who's killed before and has no problem doing it again...<br /><br />I have always loved this series and this book isn't any different. It brings me back to Stella Maris Island, just outside Charleston, South Carolina, where Liz and her family lives. We're once again drawn into their lives, along with Liz's teenage friend Colleen, who died when she was seventeen and is guardian of the island. But Colleen's main mission is to protect the island from people who would ruin it, and Liz is only one step in that direction. With only Liz and Nate able to see her, it makes things difficult when she's around.<br /><br />Liz and Nate have to don disguises to find the information they're looking for, and that includes attending Murray's funeral, where they encounter three women who all insist they were his girlfriend. Finding out that Murray had more layers to him than they thought, they also discover that his current girlfriend Annalise may have been closer to him than anyone. But someone wanted him out of the way, enough to destroy any evidence there might have been. And with what they find out, Annalise might be another target unless they can surreptitiously help her, too. <br /><br />Among the investigation keeping them busy, Liz discovers that her friend Sonny Ravenel, is heading the police investigation, and he knows something's up with her brother Blake, police chief of Stella Maris. Blake and his girlfriend Poppy have just taken a much-needed vacation, but Sonny refuses to discuss it. Liz, with her natural curiosity, born of the fact of her job, is wondering what's up. But she doesn't have time to worry about it when her mother calls and tells her to find out what's going on with her father -- he's having packages delivered to the house and won't tell her what they are. So Liz, naturally, now has to delve into that somehow while working the murder case.<br /><br />What follows is a tale of murder, greed, larceny, and lies. Liz and Nate discover more than they expected, and it brings things out into the open that have been hidden without a clue to the truth. There is more to the story, and more people involved than they first expected, It sets forth a chain of events that could cost Liz things she values most; and brings a sadness along with great joy for her.<br /><br />There is also a hilarious scene between her mother, father, and a horrendous surprise by her father that while funny as can be, almost sets her mother's teeth on edge and when the rest of the family finds out, they're all on her side. Just that one scene alone is worth reading the book.<br /><br />Since I would love to say more but refuse to give away any major spoilers, I must end this review with what I have already said. When the murderer is found out and everything comes together, it is more than a satisfying story, and it makes it difficult to wait for the next in the series. Highly recommended.<br /><br />I received an advance copy from the publisher and Edelweiss, but this in no way influenced my review.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8327470433650269956" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer3513423104" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3019377522952992910">This is the ninth book in what I’ll always think of as my Pandemic Series. They were fast, fun books that didn’t require a lot of concentration. Same characters throughout all of them that felt like friends when I wasn’t seeing my real friends because of the virus. There is one more, a Christmas themed book just released, which I hope will help get me through an altered season.</span>

  <span id="freeText15133186871491169971" style="display:none">I think that this book is the best in the series so far. As always, Susan keeps you guessing throughout the book with twists and turns, all while keeping you laughing at the antics of the main character’s family. The plot moves along at a good pace without sacrificing details. You’ll also get a whole new list of wonderful stops to make the next time you’re in Charleston. I don’t want to give away a single detail-but I will admit that I read this in one sitting! I couldn’t put it down and it felt as if it flew by! <br /><br />I would like to thank Eidelweiss, Henery Press, and the author for the advanced reader copy of this book and the opportunity to review it.</span>

It’s so great when a book you have been waiting for lives up to your hopes. This is the ninth Liz Talbot mystery. I think I can work as a stand alone, but really good if you have been following along on Liz and Nate’s adventures. When I read these books I feel as if I am catching up with old friends. This time Liz and Nate are investigating the murder of he uncle of one of a group of three young men who are trying to get a hemp farm off the ground. The case is rife with suspects, so Liz and Nate, along with ghost, Colleen, have their hands full. The Charleston setting along with food descriptions lend atmosphere. Liz’s family provides comic relief. I love this series. </span>

<div id="review_3417302806" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3417302806" />
    <a title="RO G&#39;ma" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/31899006-ro-g-ma"><img alt="RO G&#39;ma" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1431217471p2/31899006.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3417302806?book_show_action=true">Jun 29, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="RO G&#39;ma" class="user" itemprop="url" name="RO G&#39;ma" href="/user/show/31899006-ro-g-ma">RO G&#39;ma</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/53451215-lowcountry-boondoggle">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31899006-ro-g-ma?shelf=2020-craving-for-cozies-challenge">2020-craving-for-cozies-challenge</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31899006-ro-g-ma?shelf=read-in-2020">read-in-2020</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3417302806" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9396104814198582055">Lowcountry Boondoggle is the ninth book in Susan Boyer’s Liz Talbot Mystery series. Ms. Boyer provides enough character background that this book can be read as a standalone. This easy read moves along at a steady pace, providing readers with a well-crafted and complex mystery, well-developed characters, Southern charm, humorous situations, and just a touch of paranormal. The book grabs readers’ attention at the beginning, and they are taken on a roller coaster ride that concludes with a surpris</span>
  <span id="freeText9396104814198582055" style="display:none">Lowcountry Boondoggle is the ninth book in Susan Boyer’s Liz Talbot Mystery series. Ms. Boyer provides enough character background that this book can be read as a standalone. This easy read moves along at a steady pace, providing readers with a well-crafted and complex mystery, well-developed characters, Southern charm, humorous situations, and just a touch of paranormal. The book grabs readers’ attention at the beginning, and they are taken on a roller coaster ride that concludes with a surprise ending. There are plenty of twists and turns and red herrings, and no shortage of suspects to keep readers engaged.<br /><br />Liz Talbot and her husband, Nate Andrews, are private investigators who live in Stella Maris, South Carolina. Liz’s high school friend, Colleen, is a ghost, and Liz and Nate are the only ones who can see and communicate with her. Colleen is the island’s guardian angel, and her assignment is to protect Stella Maris, but she looks out for Liz and Nate as well. Liz’s family adds humor to everyone’s life. Darius Baker’s recently discovered son, Brantley Miller, has gone into the hemp farm business with two of his college friends, Tyler Hamilton and Will Caper. When a beloved Charleston professor, Dr. Murray Hamilton, is murdered, Liz and Nate are asked to look into the death and clear Brantley of any involvement his death. Prior to his death, Brantley and two of his college friends, Tyler Duval and Will Capers, approached Dr. Hamilton, who is Tyson’s uncle, to invest in their hemp farm, but he turned them down. Unfortunately, the murder occurred after Brantley, Tyson, and Will asked Dr. Hamilton to invest in their business, and Tyson becomes a prime suspect because he stands to inherit a substantial amount of money, but Brantley and Will are suspects as well. As always, Liz and Nate, who are well organized and methodical in their investigations, leave no stone unturned as they diligently work to discover the truth.<br /><br />I received an Advance Reader Copy of this book from Edelweiss/Above the Treeline and voluntarily reviewed it.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="9396104814198582055" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17074498-carla-johnson-hicks?shelf=cozy-mystery">cozy-mystery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17074498-carla-johnson-hicks?shelf=eidelwiess">eidelwiess</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3549208200" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9547467419442386984">Once again, I enjoyed my visit to Stella Maris, South Carolina. Catching up with PIs, Liz Talbot, her husband Nate and their friends and families is always interesting. In this outing, Liz and Nate are hired by celebrity Darius Baker to prove that his newly discovered son, was not involved in either his adoptive family's death nor the death of his friend's uncle. Brantley and two of his friends are starting up a Hemp Farm to sell the stems to make parts for technology. They have been trying to r</span>
  <span id="freeText9547467419442386984" style="display:none">Once again, I enjoyed my visit to Stella Maris, South Carolina. Catching up with PIs, Liz Talbot, her husband Nate and their friends and families is always interesting. In this outing, Liz and Nate are hired by celebrity Darius Baker to prove that his newly discovered son, was not involved in either his adoptive family's death nor the death of his friend's uncle. Brantley and two of his friends are starting up a Hemp Farm to sell the stems to make parts for technology. They have been trying to round up investors and Professor Hamilton had recently turned them down. As it turns out, there are others who may have wanted him dead, so Liz, Nate and ghostly friend Colleen set out to find the killer.<br /><br />I always enjoy Liz and Nate’s adventures. This is the ninth book in the series, but it can be read as a standalone. You will miss some character development on the personal side of the characters, but you will still be able to enjoy this story. Susan Boyer does a great job balancing the characters personal lives and the mystery. I enjoy the many quirky characters that we meet in these stories, although this one follows Liz and Nate more closely than some of the others. There is always some humour in these stories and this one is no exception. I love how Nate and Liz look out for each other, but also have the same concerns and disagreements that other married couples have. The mystery is well-plotted with some red herrings that kept me guessing. I did figure out who the killer was just before the reveal, and there was quite a twist at the end. Another well written story by Susan M. Boyer. I definitely recommend this series, especially if you enjoy a southern setting in your mystery. I was gifted a copy of this book upon request. The rating and opinions shared are my own.</span>

And as usual I'm looking forward to what is next for Liz & Nate. I don't want to share any spoilers for those who haven't read the series or this book but you may want to have some tissues handy because this one had me in my feelin</span>
  <span id="freeText15033575819285455468" style="display:none">Susan does it again! I am a sucker for the lowcountry mysteries and have come to love Liz and Nate (and Colleen). Full of the usual mystery and suspense you'd expect coupled with the awesomeness that is Liz's family, this one had me turning pages until the very end... And as usual I'm looking forward to what is next for Liz &amp; Nate. I don't want to share any spoilers for those who haven't read the series or this book but you may want to have some tissues handy because this one had me in my feelings, too. Thank you to Edelweiss, the author and publisher for my advanced review copy. All opinions and thoughts are my own.</span>

I have called Charleston home for 5 years and love the accurate detail Susan puts into her books about the city, the culture, and food.   <span id="freeText7074311067687897659" style="display:none">Thank you to Edelweiss, Susan M. Boyer, and the publisher for my advanced review copy. This review is totally my own.<br /><br />I love most book set in the Lowcountry and have been a big fan of the Liz Talbot Mystery series from Book 1. I have called Charleston home for 5 years and love the accurate detail Susan puts into her books about the city, the culture, and food. I have discovered many new restaurants through her books, even though I live here. I'll be trying Cru very soon. =)<br /><br />All of the Liz Talbot books are very fast paced and exciting, Boondoggle is no exception. I couldn't put it down and stayed up until 5AM to finish it in one day. From the beginning, I was trying to figure out "who dunnit" and was completely surprised by the outcome. Liz and Nate, their family, and friends are such characters...unique, endearing, and believable. <br /><br />At one point, I believe that this was planned to be the final novel in the series. That would've made me so sad because there are obviously many more tales to be told. I'm thrilled this won't be the end of the road for Stella Maris and its charming inhabitants. <br /></span>

<div id="review_3413383984" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3413383984" />
    <a title="B" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/33907606-b"><img alt="B" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3413383984?book_show_action=true">Jun 27, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="B" class="user" itemprop="url" name="B" href="/user/show/33907606-b">B</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/53451215-lowcountry-boondoggle">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3413383984" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12589467080707568771">I was anxiously awaiting Lowcountry Boondoggle, the 9th book in Susan Boyer's Lowcountry cozy mystery series, set in Stella Maris, a fictional island near Charleston. It's her best book yet, though it can easily be read as a stand alone mystery. Another home run for Susan Boyer!<br/><br/>PIs Liz & Nate continue their work for their client Darius, investigating the death of a local professor. Professor was the uncle of Darius' son Brantley's business partner, Tyler. Brantley, Tyler & Will were partners in </span>
  <span id="freeText12589467080707568771" style="display:none">I was anxiously awaiting Lowcountry Boondoggle, the 9th book in Susan Boyer's Lowcountry cozy mystery series, set in Stella Maris, a fictional island near Charleston. It's her best book yet, though it can easily be read as a stand alone mystery. Another home run for Susan Boyer!<br /><br />PIs Liz &amp; Nate continue their work for their client Darius, investigating the death of a local professor. Professor was the uncle of Darius' son Brantley's business partner, Tyler. Brantley, Tyler &amp; Will were partners in a start-up hemp business. The night before the professor died, the 3 young men had dinner in the professor's home. Tyler tried to convince his uncle/professor to invest -did the professor die for declining the opportunity? Was the professor's home blown up to eliminate security camera footage or evidence related to his death? Was Brantley, who had legal trouble the prior year, a suspect because of his past? Darius asked Liz &amp; Nate to investigate &amp; if not guilty, clear these young men of suspicion by the police<br /><br />Was relationship jealousy the reason for the professor's death? Four of the professor's current &amp; prior girlfriends came to his viewing &amp; funeral, surprising family and friends with their antics. Was the current girlfriend jealous of the professor's relationship with his best friend of 30 years? Was the bestfriend jealous of the time the new girlfriend spent with his old friend, the professor?<br /><br />Did cheating students kill the professor to protect their academic success? The professor caught Keith, his niece's husband, in a "compromising situation" in a local bar; did the he kill the professor to protect his secret? <br /><br />Did the professor's murderer want to silence Liz &amp; Nate for investigating not only his murder, but others from the prior book? Many plot twists &amp; connections keep the book interesting and difficult to put down, but not confusing. <br /><br />Boyer's quirky characters &amp; their ongoing antics, including Liz's parents and siblings, make me feel I'm coming home to family. Several surprises happen to Liz's family, which was fun to read! Liz &amp; Nate's relationship grows deeper with each book. Can't wait to see the family celebration Nate is planning for their first wedding anniversary in the next book? Write faster Susan Boyer-I can't wait!<br /><br />Thanks to Henery Press &amp; Susan Boyer's team for the advanced reader copy-I read it in one sitting, then reread to savor the details! Susan's books are a pleasure to read with the interesting plots &amp; quirky characters who've grown close to my heart over the series, including pets &amp; a supernatural spirit from Liz's childhood! I recommend this well crafted mystery, along with the other 8 in the Lowcountry Series-fun beach reads so fill up your kindle before your next vacation or staycation! </span>
  <a data-text-id="12589467080707568771" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3374905734" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15124440497552892498">Susan Boyer’s Liz Talbot mysteries are always well-written and well-plotted. Lowcountry Boondoggle is no exception. I highly recommend this book.<br/><br/>Darius Baker’s son, Brantley, has gone into a hemp farm business with two of his college friends, Tyler Hamilton and Will Caper. Murray, Ty’s uncle, is a beloved local college professor. Someone killed him and then his house blew up. Unfortunately, the murder occurred after Ty, Brantley, and Will asked Murray to invest in their business and he declined.</span>
  <span id="freeText15124440497552892498" style="display:none">Susan Boyer’s Liz Talbot mysteries are always well-written and well-plotted. Lowcountry Boondoggle is no exception. I highly recommend this book.<br /><br />Darius Baker’s son, Brantley, has gone into a hemp farm business with two of his college friends, Tyler Hamilton and Will Caper. Murray, Ty’s uncle, is a beloved local college professor. Someone killed him and then his house blew up. Unfortunately, the murder occurred after Ty, Brantley, and Will asked Murray to invest in their business and he declined. Now Ty is a prime suspect because of the money he will inherit. Brantley and Will are also suspects. Liz and Nate are hired to solve the murder and hopefully clear Ty and his partners.<br /><br />There’s no shortage of suspects in this case. Did Brantley or Will kill Murray over money? Or did his current girlfriend kill him because of jealousy? Maybe it was one of his previous girlfriends? Then again, Murray had issues with several students. Could they have killed him? Will Caper’s grandfather, whose land they were using for the hemp farm, was also a suspect. Or was it Ty’s sister, Flannery, or Flannery’s husband?<br /><br />In addition to investigating the main murder mystery, we see Liz and Nate struggling with several personal issues. We also get to enjoy Liz’s wacky and wonderful family, who has a few surprises they share. Finally, we’re again treated to a detailed view of Charleston, South Carolina. We walk the various streets with Liz and Nate and, even better, hear about all the wonderful food they eat. <br />Lowcountry Boondoggle is a solid, 5-star mystery. I loved it! After so many books, the main characters feel like old friends. You cheer their good news and mourn their bad news. Oh and once again, I failed to guess “whodunit!” <br /><br />Thank you to the author and publisher for a review copy.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer1162790888599487859">Lowcountry Boondoggle, the ninth and latest mystery novel in her Lowcountry series, is Susan Boyer’s love song to Stella Maris and Liz and Nate. <br/><br/>They are the private investigators who provide the spice that makes the books, especially this one, tingle with so much excitement and anticipation that you can’t stop reading until the end.<br/><br/>Client Darius Baker again needs help proving his son Brantley and friend Ty did not kill Ty’s Uncle Murray (Professor) Hamilton or bomb and burn up his house.<br/><br/>Brantle</span>
  <span id="freeText1162790888599487859" style="display:none">Lowcountry Boondoggle, the ninth and latest mystery novel in her Lowcountry series, is Susan Boyer’s love song to Stella Maris and Liz and Nate. <br /><br />They are the private investigators who provide the spice that makes the books, especially this one, tingle with so much excitement and anticipation that you can’t stop reading until the end.<br /><br />Client Darius Baker again needs help proving his son Brantley and friend Ty did not kill Ty’s Uncle Murray (Professor) Hamilton or bomb and burn up his house.<br /><br />Brantley, Ty and friend Will are partners in a hemp farming business and Hamilton had just refused them a business loan.<br /><br />Liz and Nate investigate the murder alongside Charleston Detective Sonny Ravenel<br />(Stella Maris is an island right near that city).<br /><br />Liz and her loving family and friends, as usual, provide comic relief: flighty ghost Colleen who flits in and out trying to help, Police Chief brother Blake and girlfriend Poppy, sister Merry and boyfriend Joe, and Daddy Frank who drives Mamma Carolyn batty at times, and hound dog, Chumley.<br /><br />Professor Hamilton had a bevy of girlfriends from dating websites like eharmony and a real one, Annalise Mitchell. Also a best friend of 30 years, Professor Pierce Fishburne.<br /><br />Ty has a sister, Flannery. Hamilton raised them after their parents’ deaths. Their uncle discovered Flannery’s husband Keith Laurens with another woman.<br /><br />Hamilton also found out that two longtime students John Porcher and Dean Johnson had been cheating.<br /><br />That gave Liz and Nate plenty to investigate.<br /><br />I was given an electronic copy of this book to read to review from Edelweiss. The opinions expressed are my own.<br /><br />I absolutely loved every word. Susan’s writing gets better and better with every book as do her stories. I think you’ll love this adventure as much as I did!</span>

Liz and her husband/partner use an amazing number of disguises and electronic gear to assist in their investigations which adds to the interest in the story.   <span id="freeText7133320068676635133" style="display:none">An excellent mystery and the descriptions of the food that gets eaten along the way will make your mouth water as you join the main characters in solving a complicated murder. Liz and her husband/partner use an amazing number of disguises and electronic gear to assist in their investigations which adds to the interest in the story. Their relationship, combining a business partnership with marriage, and the complications that can occur are addressed in this book, adding an extra dimension to the action that evolves. And, as usual, though we see less of them in this book, Liz's family is a hoot.<br /><br />The author has a real talent for creating very believable characters that you learn to care about, especially the main victim. There is an unexpected conclusion to one mystery that I didn't see coming and some questions at the end about Liz's other-worldly "assistant," Colleen, that was unsettling. Colleen added her own comic relief to these books so I certainly hope the series continues with her. Plus, we need to find out what happens as regards Liz's reoccurring dream.<br /><br />"I was hit again with how sad it was that Murray, who smelled the roses every day, has been yanked out of a life lived so fully. He'd reveled in life's simpler pleasures—lunch with a friend, tea with a loved one, burgers and mentoring young men. … Whoever had blown out Murray Hamilton's candle, I was determined to see to it they paid for that." Whew! No villain in their right mind wants Liz after them.<br /><br />Nice job, Ms. Boyer. I look forward to the next book in the series. Love the cover too! It is like the epitome of cozy covers.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer9833260013078765455">I just finished reading an advance review copy of Susan M. Boyers’ latest Liz Talbot book, Lowcountry Boondoggle. Thanks to Edelweiss, the author and publisher! All thoughts are my own. Those who are fans of great mysteries will not be disappointed! Susan has given us another great installment from the lives of Liz and Nate and the Talbot family. This book has some great twists and turns and kept me guessing until the end. Just the kind of mystery I enjoy! For those who have never read a Liz Tal</span>
  <span id="freeText9833260013078765455" style="display:none">I just finished reading an advance review copy of Susan M. Boyers’ latest Liz Talbot book, Lowcountry Boondoggle. Thanks to Edelweiss, the author and publisher! All thoughts are my own. Those who are fans of great mysteries will not be disappointed! Susan has given us another great installment from the lives of Liz and Nate and the Talbot family. This book has some great twists and turns and kept me guessing until the end. Just the kind of mystery I enjoy! For those who have never read a Liz Talbot mystery, I would highly recommend you get started! Liz and Nate are private investigators who live on the island of Stella Maris in the low country of South Carolina. Susan writes her books in such a way that you feel like you’re there with Liz and Nate and are listening in, just like Liz’s ghostly sidekick, Colleen. These books are great mysteries with a lot of humor - I found myself laughing out loud! Liz’ family add such color and humor to the books. Boondoggle can certainly stand alone if you’ve not yet started the series, but even if you read this one first, I suggest you read the entire series! All of these books are wonderful, well-written and keep you engaged. Like all of Susan’s books, this one was hard to put this down! I hated for it to end and can’t wait for the next installment! These characters are so great, you feel like you’re missing old friends and can’t wait to catch up on all that’s happened since you last got together! If you love mysteries, grab this one! You won’t be disappointed!</span>

  <span id="freeText1055620034979463162" style="display:none">This is a great series and each book gets better and better! And as is Susan Boyer's style, you are grabbed from the beginning and taken on a roller coaster ride until the surprise ending with a little humor thrown in! When PIs Liz and Nate along with Liz's Ghostly BFF, Colleen are asked to look into the murder of a local professor. Who could have done it. We are taken on a wild goose chase from red-herring to red-herring. This may hit a little too close to home for Darius a TV celebrity. Could it have been his son, Brantley who was trying to make a go of the hemp business? We are treated to the eccentric cast of Stella Maris residents including Brantley and his two business partners, college buddies, Tyler and Will. The professor just happened to be Tyler's uncle and Tyler stands to inherit a sizeable amount of money from his uncle that Tyler could invest in their hemp business since his uncle, when asked, declined to invest. With lots of suspects and the explosion of the professor's house destroying evidence Liz and Nate are going to have a rough time figuring this one out. This case with Liz and Nate will keep you turning pages. Once you begin you won't be able to put this book down until you have finished. I receive and ARC from the author but the opinions expressed here are strictly my own!</span>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3383833533" />
    <a title="Mary Lou" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/57351655-mary-lou"><img alt="Mary Lou" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_50x66-632230dc9882b4352d753eedf9396530.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3383833533?book_show_action=true">Jun 09, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mary Lou" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mary Lou" href="/user/show/57351655-mary-lou">Mary Lou</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3383833533" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1230463549038718513">Susan M. Boyer and her Lowcountry series have captured my interest and love of Charleston and surrounding area, and Lowcountry Boondoggle, her latest book in this wonderful series, did not disappoint. Nate and Liz continue their PI endeavors, investigating the death of a professor from the College of Charleston. Their very thorough and detailed investigative approach in helping their client, leads to many people and motives; could the son of Darius, their neighbor on Stella Maris and their clien</span>
  <span id="freeText1230463549038718513" style="display:none">Susan M. Boyer and her Lowcountry series have captured my interest and love of Charleston and surrounding area, and Lowcountry Boondoggle, her latest book in this wonderful series, did not disappoint. Nate and Liz continue their PI endeavors, investigating the death of a professor from the College of Charleston. Their very thorough and detailed investigative approach in helping their client, leads to many people and motives; could the son of Darius, their neighbor on Stella Maris and their client, really be guilty? The great writing and incredible imagination of the author, and her detailed knowledge of the Lowcountry, the wonderful city of Charleston and their incredible restaurants, treats the reader to suspense, laughter....and to me ... some tears. I have been hooked on Susan’s books from the first in the series, Lowcountry Boil. Each book is a standalone, but I highly recommend beginning with the first one. Liz has a great family living on Stella Maris, and you will fall in love with her parents. Liz’s father once again, with his “good intentions”, will have you laughing out loud. Susan Boyer has done it again! Thank you to Edelweiss, the author and publisher for an advanced review copy. </span>
  <a data-text-id="1230463549038718513" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3463051919?book_show_action=true">Aug 22, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kay Hudson" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kay Hudson" href="/user/show/34263831-kay-hudson">Kay Hudson</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/34263831-kay-hudson?shelf=mystery">mystery</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3463051919" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15134519957483168936"><i>Lowcountry Boondoggle</i> is Susan M. Boyer’s ninth Liz Talbot mystery, and once again the city of Charleston and the South Carolina barrier islands are a fascinating part of the story. This time around, Liz and her husband/partner are drawn into a case by a former client, Darius Baker (<i>Lowcountry Boomerang</i>), whose recently-discovered son, Brantley, has become involved in a hemp farming operation. Nothing wrong with that, until the uncle of one of Brantley’s two partners is murdered and his house de</span>
  <span id="freeText15134519957483168936" style="display:none"><i>Lowcountry Boondoggle</i> is Susan M. Boyer’s ninth Liz Talbot mystery, and once again the city of Charleston and the South Carolina barrier islands are a fascinating part of the story. This time around, Liz and her husband/partner are drawn into a case by a former client, Darius Baker (<i>Lowcountry Boomerang</i>), whose recently-discovered son, Brantley, has become involved in a hemp farming operation. Nothing wrong with that, until the uncle of one of Brantley’s two partners is murdered and his house destroyed in a gas explosion.<br /><br />Was the hemp operation involved? The uncle, a university professor, had declined to invest. What about all those women who showed up at the professor’s funeral? Or the cloud over Brantley’s head—could he have set the fire that killed his adoptive family? And then there were two of the professor’s students, possibly involved in something shady. Not only are there plenty of suspects, the suspects are suspicious of one another.<br /><br /><i>Lowcountry Boondoggle</i> is another wild ride for Liz and Nate, not to mention the continuing adventures of Liz’s family, what with her father’s over-the-top Halloween yard decor and a couple of surprises from her brother Blake. I’ve enjoyed this series from the beginning, and this installment did not let me down.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15134519957483168936" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('JhgQ5Qj3kcv0RtXdflOWyWO7Dd5fXEIXTx8gxaxsrYbJeGmQF/5hMQBOHMEeH5vTsUSaBpP1s1LsYECMmo1ItA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('IId1fujnwylBJIu36Rk1DvkXr83Hxz5gLfq3PM5rWuHP5wwL9+4z07UsQquJVTgUK+g4FQtuzyWOhdd1+Iq/0w==')})
  }

And buy more insurance, lots more; I’ve got a friend named Stanley.   FROM THE PREFACE:   It is perhaps unorthodox to declare a story which transpired 6-8 years ago in the country’s largest metropolis historical fiction but labelling it otherwise would be a deception. The election of a bilious talk show host to the world’s highest office, the NSA-sponsored surveillance, cataloging and storage of millions of Americans’ phone logs and recordings, the petulant, self-imposed withdrawal of Great Britain from the EU, the global contagion of anti-immigrant nationalism – no pundit could have predicted these developments in 2013. And no one would have believed him.  I intended this book as a work of contemporary fiction. It described, I think accurately, the city and world I lived in. Just six years have elapsed since its completion, but I might as well have described ancient China. The world and New York City of 2013 no longer exist. Her play &quot;The Lonely Road&quot; won her a coveted spot in Dr. Pierce Baker\'s Harvard 47 Workshop in New York. While in New York, she went undercover to report on her findings of &quot;getting on the stage of New York&quot; (Broadway) under the guise of a pseudonym. While in New York, she worked for the Newspaper Enterprise Association (N.E.A.). She interviewed well-known celebrities of the era including authors including Richard Atwater (Mr. Poppers Penguins) and Dorothy Parker (and the Algonquin Round Table), actors including Will Rogers, philanthropists, Broadway chorus girls, sports heroes, circus performers and many more. Additionally, she joined the Blue Pencil Club, an elite literary society of only a handful of members the same year as author H.P. Lovecraft.\n\nHer column &quot;Demi-Tasse and Mrs. Grundy&quot; won praise from her readers nationwide. She went on to become a successful society page editor for the Akron Beacon Journal in Akron, Ohio between 1924-1927, when she passed away suddenly at the age of 33 after childbirth complications. Her passing devastated her readers. Her followers begged her husband Bill to one day make a book of all her stories, but none was ever made – until now. \n\nAlmost a century later, her great-granddaughter, Kristin (née Carter) Groulx, also a writer, historian and genealogist, has taken the time to thumb through saved newspaper clippings and put them to paper in one book for Josephine’s beloved readers to see and remember her   <span id="freeText12232067123170820069" style="display:none"><b>
  <i>Susan M. Boyer</i>
</b> is the author of the USA TODAY bestselling Liz Talbot mystery series. She was blessed with a quintessential small-town childhood and has had a life-long love affair with books. Susan is grateful to have been gifted with an over-active imagination. She was one of those children whose teachers were always telling her mamma that her talents needed to be "channeled." She's been making things up and writing them down her whole life<br /><br />Susan’s debut novel, Lowcountry Boil, won the 2012 Agatha Award for Best First Novel, the Daphne du Maurier Award for Excellence in Mystery/Suspense, and garnered several other award nominations. The third book in the series, Lowcountry Boneyard, was a Spring 2015 Southern Independent Booksellers Alliance Okra Pick, and was short-listed for the 2016 Pat Conroy Beach Music Mystery Prize.<br /><br />Lowcountry Book Club was a Summer 2016 SIBA Okra Pick and was short-listed for the 2017 Southern Book Prize in Mystery &amp; Detective Fiction.<br /><br />Lowcountry Boondoggle, book 9 in the series, was released June 30, 2020. LOWCOUNTRY BOUGHS OF HOLLY, book 10, will be released on November 17, 2020.<br /><br />Susan loves beaches, Southern food, and small towns where everyone knows everyone, and everyone has crazy relatives. You’ll find all of the above in her novels. She lives in Greenville, SC, with her husband and an inordinate number of houseplants.<br /><br /><br />To learn more about Susan, visit susanmboyer.com</span>
